▲国货维持会 中华国货维持会常务委员汪星一、王介安，昨天电呈中央党部国民政府各机关说，（抬头略）东邻日本，虎视东亚，久怀吞并东三省等的野心，处心积虑，路人皆知。如今竟于万宝山事件，煽动朝鲜民众酿成暴动，残杀华侨，其幕后真相洞然，令人发指。查朝鲜本是我国藩属，以该国党祸，借口我国保护不力，引起甲午之役，遂其割取朝鲜的贪婪欲望。然而当年朝鲜的混乱不如今日之甚，且并未发生戕害日本民众之事，而日本人已肆意施展其泼辣手段。今风潮如此扩大，华人被害如此之重，日本政府既无节制及约束朝鲜民众的能力，也无保障及维护华侨的设施。我政府亟应提出重大抗议，（一）要求日本政府放弃对朝鲜的管辖权，既然其为独立国，一切境内政治法律税捐，由朝鲜人自理，不由日本人代为筹划。（一）在上述条件未成立以前，先由中日韩三国，订立平等商约，实行互惠。凡是华货日货运往朝鲜的，待遇一律，不得由日本一国

Page 14

垄断。华货久销朝鲜，历史悠久。二十年来，被日本的重税所排斥，属会屡次收到旅韩侨商的声明，近十年来，受到进口苛税的重大束缚，仅就华绸方面来说，从前只征收货价百分之五的税，那时华货在朝鲜销路极盛。继后陆续加税，增至货价百分之三四十时，华绸仍有半数可以销售。民国十二年又加至货价百分之百，一百日绸运到韩国，仅征收货价百分之八的税，两相比较，何止天壤之别。最终导致每年销往朝鲜一千数百万金的华绸，从此绝迹。上年新订的中日协定，虽减少了百分之三十，然对改变时艰毫无补益，迄今依然寸货不能运往。故近来华商在朝鲜的商业，只能经营日货，情状实在可怜。今又狼心日甚，愈演愈烈，初则仇视华货，扼其咽喉，征以重税，使其不能进口，残害华侨的商业地位，无所不用其极。彼之封销政策，目的既达，近又仇视华民，挑拨朝鲜民众，大肆屠杀。我国若不提出严重要求，势将以道歉和抚恤金敷衍了事，还成什么国际社会？以治标而言，（一）我国政府应用相当方法，务使朝鲜的骚乱不再发生。（二）迅速运用外交政策，恢复在朝鲜的中国国权，使华侨在朝鲜得以永久的保障。（三）中央暗派大员周密调查被害伤民及财产损失，要求日本政府赔偿，以免调查时被日军警借口保护，实行包围。（四）重惩保护不力的日韩军警。以治本而言，（一）朝鲜恢复国权，订立中日韩通商平等条约，实行税率平等。凡是日货运往中国，华货运往日本，以及运入朝鲜境内的，彼此一律平等，实行互惠，悉照日货同等税率纳税征收，不得再将华货征收重税。盖此项约章，关系着华侨在朝鲜的生死存亡，故须提前要求订定。（二）东三省为我国领土，日本永远不得驻兵，并严厉要求撤退满铁沿线的驻军。（二）万宝山一案，关系尤其深切。凡是日韩人民，非有脱离本国国籍的确实证明，不得归化中国。既然入了华籍，日本当然不再干预。此次约中，自应妥善规定。凡此种种，是为了消除根本的大患，免除旧时藩属长期被压迫的局面，且以恢复华鲜的商业运输，于国际前途、实业前途，关系甚巨。属会在青天白日之下，素来仰赖政府以革命的精神，办理外交，一洗帝制腐化的劣败。不揣冒昧，谨本心理，缪贡刍荛。全国民众，愿为后盾。现届中日协定修约以前，大部分令饬属会会同有关系团体，共同研究，贡献出具体意见以备采择在案。除专案仍遵照办理外，并恳请钧部一并注意，合并陈明，云云。

▲闵行各界 上海县第一区闵行各界，昨天下午一时，召集全区各界代表大会，筹议切实对日办法，到商会、教育会、农会、各同业公会等十余团体，由常务沈景主席，决议立即成立反日援侨会，推举沈景、张景龄等十一人为委员。该会定今天起开始工作，对于往来船只，均须严密检查，各商店所存日货，须一律登记，停止发售，并严禁征收任何基金云。

刺宋案续讯 112

▲嫌疑人简丹已释放

▲监察院秘书足骨炸断

▲军警机关保护北站

在北站谋刺财政部长宋子文案中，昨天军警机关及捕房方面，分头缉捕凶徒，尚无结果。至于前晨汇司捕房曾在浙江路安乐旅馆拘获嫌疑人广东人简丹一名，于当日下午，移交给警备司令部侦查队。昨天据本报记者调查，侦查队因简丹的口供，虽有不符之处，但证据不足，遂即时派侦查员至宋部长公馆，详细询问宋部长及卫士等，始悉凶徒均服白色短衫，内有一人穿长衫，并无穿军衣者在内，而简丹系穿军服，经审查结果，遂于前日下午六时，将简丹一名释放。

又受伤的卫士、路警及监察院秘书王士铎等十名，在医院疗治经过，均极其良好。本报记者昨天又往福民医院访问了医院秘书王士铎君，据王称，右足伤处已用手术，弹片已取出，但右足除大足趾外，其余四足趾的节骨均断裂，将来虽不至于残废，恐怕行走方面，定会有些许困难。医生说，约一个月左右，方可痊愈出院。今天（即昨日）极感痛苦，真所谓无妄之灾，言下不胜唏嘘。又说，当枪声响起时，我在宋部长一行人的前面，身已将出车站大门，及闻警后，同行乘客，都向大门乱窜，人众拥挤，更加无法前进，命令大家急忙伏地避弹，复遭炸弹波及，也真是不幸啊。我穿的皮鞋，若足皮鞋面已洞穿，想见爆炸之力云云。

淞沪警备司令部深觉北站为京沪沪杭交通要道，警卫力量薄弱，爰于昨日起，特派本部武装士兵一连，常驻车站，以资维护。

路局方面，除已严令各分段，加紧侦缉凶犯，务求破获惩办外，以为北站及南京下关等地，是京沪来往要冲，为惩前毖后起见，拟于北站三道出入口处，增设武装岗警，常驻守卫，并派警务稽查一人，轮流督率，且遇到京中各要人来往，更准时加派长警护卫，以昭慎密。兹录两路警务长邓祖禹呈文如下：敬呈者，本月二十三日上午七时十分钟，第六次列车到上海北站后，匪徒在站抛掷炸弹，伤害旅客的情形，已于当时呈报钧局备案。查本路路警仅有少数枪支，只供押车之用，各站岗警，只持警械，维持秩序。故两路路綫，均依赖宪兵及驻军保护，南京上海各大站检查行人，也由卫戍司令部·警备司令部及地方警察办理。如上海北站检查事宜，向由淞沪警备司令部办理。于本年七月二日，曾奉钧局第七六五号训令饬知，奉淞沪警备司令部令，车站检查处，已通令撤消，关于检查行人事宜，由公安局派警办理，本部派员督率等因，公安第五区同时在本站三道出入门口，均派有三四名警察检查行人，以防不测，日日如常，本极缜密。此历来的实在情形，早在钧长洞鉴之中。昨日事变突起，各人多走避不遑，路警为职责所在，虽无器械，也奋勇分头救护。宋部长也由京一分段警长赵忠心护送至钧局楼上，以避凶锋。此出事时的情形也。查上海北站与南京两站，时有要人往来，嗣后戒备，自当加严。警务长除令京七分段金警务长田对于南京站妥为防范，上海北站，拟在三道出入口门前，加设武装岗位，常驻守卫，请发给木壳枪十支，以便应用，并请派警务稽查一名，更番督率，以示严密。再各要人往返，请钧局转请先行电示，以便准时加派长警卫护，以昭慎重，警务长戒于既往、警于将来起见，除严令京一分段及各分段加紧侦缉，以期破获正凶，依法惩办外，谨呈鉴核。

宋子文偕眷昨日赴青岛奔丧 113

▲楠木棺一口附轮运往

▲宋蔼龄宋美龄均未行

财政部长宋子文之母宋老太太，于二十三日上午十一时四十分，在青岛因病逝世，其次子宋子良随侍在侧。前日宋宅接到丧电后，即筹备一切，以重金购到最上等楠木棺材一口，并决定在沪之长子宋子文、三子宋子安、长女宋蔼龄、三女宋美龄，全体于昨晨乘坐奉天九前往青岛奔丧。事前，严守秘密，船票由日本领事署代办，大连汽船会社特派林弘技在轮船上照料一切。昨晨八时三十分，黄浦码头附近，由武装中西探捕特别警备，驱逐闲人观望。八时五十分，宋子文夫妇、宋子安，偕同江海关监督唐海安及武装卫士八人，分乘汽车，驶抵码头，宋子文并雇用俄日保镖各一名，在严重保护之下，簇拥登轮，共购头等船票九张，加上卫士等共约十余人。宋美龄宋蔼龄因病，临时未行。楠木棺一口，也附轮船前往青岛。九时正，奉天丸始解缆离沪。

王正廷避寿赴杭 114

▲转往莫干山游览

外交部长王正廷，因今日为其五十岁大庆，其友好属僚等拟凑资为其祝寿，王外长坚决辞谢未允，前晚避寿来沪。今晨九时三十分，偕其夫人公子等，乘特快列车赴杭，转往莫干山游览，预定数日内即返京。至于外传外部总务司发出通告，将寿礼一律改为收取现金，以便将此款筹办学校，以留作纪念等等，并无其事，但私人友好方面略有筹备，完全是个人行动。

陈绍宽昨访宋子文 115

▲长江防务严密

▲李氏督造军舰

海军次长兼江南造船所所长陈绍宽，昨日（二十四）晨自南京到沪，即至宋财长家探望。午後，国闻社记者晤陈氏于船所，与作谈话如下：

▲慰望宋氏 陈氏于晨间七时下车后，即换乘汽车，径赴宋宅探望，并吊唁宋老太太在青岛逝世，宋氏因心绪潦乱，故陈氏仅与谈片刻，即辞出。

▲江防严密 据陈云，海军在长江与长岳二线防务，近因赤匪偷运粮食，故沿江各地，均有军舰驻守，其他专派巡舰往来接弋。逸仙舰本日（即昨日）已离京上驶，停泊在沪港的自强与海筹两舰，日内也将开往南京驻防。现在长江一带者，九江有楚有舰，汉口有楚泰、楚谦，岳州有威胜，长沙有民权，白螺矶有顺胜、诚胜，加上本日开出的逸仙一艘，各处总计有二十余艘军舰，江防甚为巩固。

▲李氏赴日 李总务厅长世界，于本日（即昨日）晨搭日轮长崎丸东渡，同行祇有李泽一，此去完全系督造海军部向日本播麻船厂订造的宁海军舰，因该舰已定于双十节下水，故工程方面，不得不从速赶造，李氏约一日后可返回云云。

杨肇熉奉部电筹备接收法公廨 116

筹备接收上海法租界会审公廨事宜，司法院行政部已委任江苏高等法院第二分院长徐维震及沪特区地方法院院长杨肇熉二氏，会同办理。据昨日高等法院第二分院书记官长对语新声社记者云，徐院长被委任筹备接收事宜不确，行政部仅令地方法院院长杨肇熉筹备，并已奉到电令，至于何时可开始办理，及筹备之内容如何，现因协定全文尚未正式签字，故不详知云。

江海各輪通航 117

▲Resumption of Navigation by Chinese Steamers on the Yangtze

Following a suspension of navigation by China Yangtze Steamship Company vessels since May 17th, lasting for two months, due to successive victories in the central government's bandit suppression campaign and a reduced need for over twenty ships for transport, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, seeking to resume steamer services on the Yangtze, dispatched Guo Waifeng to Nanchang to personally petition Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, requesting the return of leased vessels. Chiang granted permission and ordered the Communications Department to return the vessels of the China Merchants Sanbei Company to their respective bureaus to maintain transportation. The Jiang Da, Jiang Yu, and Jiang Xin, among other vessels, have been released to Shanghai in recent days, significantly increasing the number of Chinese steamer services, with two ships traveling between Shanghai and Hankou daily.

▲Full Resumption of Shipping in Shanghai Waters

Shipping between Shanghai and Haizhou had been disrupted due to a strike by stevedores at the docks, as well as a work stoppage by barge workers. Consequently, merchant vessels heading from Shanghai to Haizhou were obstructed at Dapu, completely halting the import and export of goods. Passenger and freight traffic from the Longhai Railway to Shanghai was also cut off. A large backlog of goods destined for Haizhou accumulated in Shanghai, and due to the ongoing boycott, there was a rush to transport Japanese goods, causing significant losses to local merchants during the week-long strike. Yesterday, a telegram arrived from Haizhou stating that the stevedores and barge workers had fully resumed work, and the obstructed vessels were unloading cargo. Shanghai was urged to expedite the transport of the accumulated goods to Haizhou.

Yesterday's Memorial for the First Anniversary of Zhao Tieqiao's Death 118

▲Public Memorial by Employees

▲Unveiling of Bronze Statue

Yesterday marked the first anniversary of the death of the late Commissioner Zhao Tieqiao of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Employees of the company, recognizing Zhao's loyalty and dedication to the country during his lifetime, as well as his significant contributions to reorganizing the company, deeply mourned his untimely assassination. To commemorate his merits, a memorial ceremony was held at 9:00 AM yesterday at the Building No. 7 1/2 on the Bund. Attendees included Mayor Zhang, former Secretary-General Xu of the Supervisory Department of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Zhou Baoli representing the Garrison Headquarters, Yuan Ludeng, Wang Bofen, and Chen Ganqing representing the Shipping Industry Association, as well as Zhao's friends Yu Huancheng, Xu Xiuzhi, Hong En, Huang Douyin, Qin Daishi, Hong Yanbin, and over four hundred others, all of whom braved the rain to attend. The Municipal Police Bureau also sent a full military band to provide music. At 9:00 AM, company employee Wang Renjing was elected chairman and reported on the statue's construction and the significance of the memorial. Commissioner Guo Waifeng then held the unveiling ceremony for the bronze statue, followed by a public memorial by company employees and the 18th branch of the Kuomintang's Third District in Shanghai. Mayor Zhang delivered a speech, stating that Commissioner Zhao's revolutionary spirit served as a model for comrades and discussed the issues of providing for his family and giving him a public burial, which should be jointly undertaken by colleagues. Yu Huancheng spoke about Zhao's lifelong dedication to the revolution, his character in breaking through constraints, and his plans to reorganize the company. Hong Yanbin then proposed three points: (1) request a public burial from the National Government; (2) request that the court investigate and announce the truth about the murderer(s) and pursue the mastermind(s); and (3) request the National Government and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to issue full pensions. All were in agreement. Finally, a representative of the family expressed gratitude, and a photograph was taken before the gathering dispersed. It is reported that Commissioner Guo of the company has decided to erect Zhao's bronze statue in the remaining space of the Yangjiadu warehouse and has designated July 24th as the company's permanent memorial day.

▲Memorial Oration by Employees

On this 24th day of July in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the staff of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, in a united memorial meeting, respectfully offer these flowers and wine to the image of the late commissioner, Zhao Tieqiao. The words read: Alas, the talented are envied by ghosts, and the rough jade is attacked by axes. Good cannot overcome evil. We have lost Commissioner Zhao. Recalling his life, a remarkable revolutionary, a youthful talent with fervent patriotism, he stirred up his sleeves in Chengdu, shedding hot blood, growing more resolute in defeat. He bid farewell to his hometown, traveling north to Yanjing, advocating alliance, and promoting northern strength. The Party's prestige flourished, his name alongside Wang Jingwei and Huang Xing. He assisted Sun Yat-sen, a wise judge of men, entrusting him with important responsibilities, to oppose Yuan Shikai and protect the Constitution, participating in battles and responding to Wuchang and Chongqing, leading troops and strategizing. Through smoke and rain of bullets, he treated honors like floating clouds, with unyielding spirit and unwavering virtue. After the revolution's success and the establishment of the capital in Nanjing, he took charge of saving the situation and reforming the shipping administration, shouldering the responsibility with courage. He reformed the decaying, overcoming adversity and startling the wealthy and powerful into flight, eliminating abuses and restoring vitality. For three years he toiled, gathering public resentment, with rumors flying and impeachment accusations pouring in. Helplessly, the water cleared to reveal the stones. Why such cruelty? The treacherous plotters, a family exterminated with their roots cut. A rapid succession of attacks. Alas, Commissioner Zhao, a revolutionary for life, died not at the hands of the enemy, nor in battle, but was killed while working hard to build. He ultimately sacrificed himself for the country and achieved benevolence. All men must die, but his spirit will live on. Remembering his past virtue, his love for the masses, his sincerity, his protection of employees, his care for them as brothers. Recalling the tragedy, we are filled with grief. A year has passed, but the injustice remains unaddressed. Who killed this loyal man? Who masterminded this ghostly plot? Those vile criminals should be brought to justice. What more can be said if the ringleader escapes? May his spirit, so mighty, strip away their wicked souls. Alas, Commissioner Zhao, a hero in life, a martyr for the nation in death. For thousands of years, his glory will shine. The Yangtze flows on, the mountains of Sichuan stand tall. The cuckoo cries blood, summoning his sorrowful soul. Soul, oh soul, accept this libation. Alas, may you enjoy the offering. (The memorial oration from the 18th branch of the Kuomintang's Third District is omitted.)

▲Current Situation of His Family

Yesterday, Zhao's wife was unwell and temporarily asked her relative, Mr. Yang Yifu, to bring her five orphaned children, including Guangzu, to the scene. Afterwards, a reporter from the Huadong News Agency interviewed Mr. Yang about the recent situation of Zhao's family. According to Mr. Yang, Zhao's family has been facing hardship recently. During Commissioner Li's time, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company granted 3,000 yuan in pension, and during Commissioner Cai's time, they supplemented it to 5,000 taels. However, with a family of several relying on it for living expenses, coupled with the fact that Zhao had incurred many debts during his life, they have been struggling. The pension stipulated by the National Government has not been received either, making the future difficult. Zhao left behind eight orphaned children: Guangfu, Guangshi, Guangli, Guangzhen, Guangxiang, and two daughters, Xinglan and Yinhai, who are all young and unable to support themselves. Therefore, they earnestly hope that the government authorities will provide assistance to Zhao's orphaned children so that they can be properly taken care of.

Guangzhao Public Association Remits Funds to Relieve Guangdong Flood 119

▲Initial Remittance of 10,000 Yuan

The Shanghai Guangzhao Public Association received a telegram from Guangdong stating that the floods were widespread and severe, requesting assistance in relief efforts. The association has remitted an initial sum of 10,000 yuan to the Guangdong Flood Relief Association for relief efforts.

Situation of Disaster Relief in Jiangxi 120

The Shanghai Society for Raising Funds for Emergency Relief in Jiangxi received telegrams yesterday from disaster investigation officers Wei Keqiang and Wu Jiasan, addressed to Wang Yilao, Wen Lanlao, Wang Xiaolao, Chairman Wang, Xu Jinglao of the Jiangxi Emergency Relief Society, and members of the presidium. The telegrams stated that they had arrived in Ganzhou, met with Commander Xiong Shihui, and requested instructions on the relief approach. He indicated that three methods had been determined: (1) Emergency Relief: establishing shelters for women, children, and students; (2) Work Relief: dividing into four lines: Ganzhou to Xinggan, Xinggan to Lean and Ningdu, Linchuan to Ningdu, and Ji'an to Ningdu; (3) Agricultural Relief: establishing agricultural cooperatives and agricultural banks. Currently, there are approximately 200,000 disaster victims in Ganzhou and over 500,000 in Ji'an. The exact number in the bandit-controlled areas is unknown. The relief plan centers on establishing shelters in Ningdu. The organization of relief efforts will be designed by the local relief departments of the party and government committees, and Wei Keqiang and Wu Jiasan have been ordered to join the work. Those in Shanghai who have pledged but not yet paid should be urged to pay in treasury bonds. As per Commander Xiong's intentions, Wang Yilao and Wang Xiaolai should quickly sell these for cash, hopefully reaching one million. The remaining funds from the Jishui Society should also be pooled together for joint cooperation. The Jishui Society was originally scheduled to send one representative, and they should be urged to come to Jiangxi to assist in the relief efforts. Wei Keqiang and Wu Jiasan were ordered to go to Ganzhou and fear they are not up to the task, and they hope for constant instructions to avoid overstepping. The remaining words are confidential. Secretary Wei Keqiang and Advisor Wu Jiasan. Wang Yilao, Wang Xiaolao, Wen Lanlao, Chairman Wang, Xu Jinglao of Jiangxi Emergency Relief Society, Yan Zhilao, presidium members, and Economic Committee members Lin and Zhang were also addressed. The eight submitted proposals have been presented to Commander Xiong. Commander Xiong stated that work relief must begin first, so that the disaster victims can be accommodated and not just sit and eat. Agricultural banks should be established urgently so that farmers can borrow and rural areas can be easily restored. It is now waiting for the allocation of funds to start. The Commander has already telegraphed Yilao, and only 5-600,000 has been remitted to Ganzhou. It is proposed to allocate 300,000 as the foundation for the Agricultural Bank and 2-300,000 for work relief and road construction, and instructed Keqiang and Jiasan to telegraph to the members for their review. Secretary Wei Keqiang and Advisor Wu Jiasan.

Report on the Investigation of the Silk Industry in Japan by the Commodity Inspection Bureau 121

▲Japanese Raw Silk Must Be Graded Before Export Is Permitted

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, in order to understand the latest situation of the silk industry in Japan, dispatched Miao Zhongxiu, director of the Raw Silk Inspection Department, accompanied by Dr. Li Yaobang, a technical officer, to Japan for investigation. They departed on the 11th of this month, arrived in Kobe on the 13th, and in the afternoon, went to the Kobe Inspection Office, where they had a very pleasant conversation with Mr. Higo of the office. Mr. Miao and Mr. Li have already informed Director Zou of the initial investigation situation by letter, generally requesting the Japanese government to prepare to implement, starting from January 1st next year, that all raw silk exports must be graded by the Kobe or Yokohama inspection offices. The trade between manufacturers and exporters must be valued according to the inspection office's grade. The Japanese government has now allocated 2 million to meet the construction and equipment needs of the Kobe and Yokohama locations. The Kobe office will set up 60 black board machines and 8 reeling machines. All needed talent will be trained by the Yokohama Inspection Office. The exporter's inspection department will cease operations next year. In the future, all Japanese raw silk exports will be inspected by the national inspection office. Japan has reached the final step.

Starting today, he will join the Chen Zhigao Law Firm at 96 Beijing Road in a cooperative partnership.

Yesterday's Hearing of Li Hefei's Granddaughter's Property Division Case 123

▲Li Mu Gong's etc. Shares in Taiping Bank

▲Court Orders Temporary Prohibition of Transfer

▲Rent from Xian Yi Li Will Be Deposited in the Bank

Li Jia Zheng, granddaughter of Li Hefei, filed a suit with the Special District Court against her stepmother after leaving her husband, Zhang Jinjiang, due to irreconcilable differences. She demanded the return of 12,000 yuan in dowry money promised by her late father's will, as well as a savings book containing 645 yuan. The court has already ruled that the plaintiff must repay 12,000 yuan, as well as interest at a rate of one percent per annum from April of this year until the date of execution. She must also return to the plaintiff a Shen Fuzhuang Juji savings book containing 645 yuan. However, Li Jia Zheng also filed a suit requesting to divide her late father's inheritance with her uncle, Mu Gong, and her brother, Jia. The court has granted her request and sealed a portion of the property located on Xianyi Road, Chongqing Road, as an attachment. However, regarding the Taiping Bank shares, the court summoned relevant parties yesterday at the Special District Court's execution chamber. The general manager of Taiping Bank testified that Li Mu Gong and others had a total of 790 shares under their names, each share worth 100 yuan, totaling 79,000 yuan. However, as of July 21st of this year, Li Chengdetang (i.e., Li Feijun) owed 39,418 yuan. The plaintiff's attorney, Ge Zhaoji, stated that according to his information, the face value of each Taiping Bank share was 1,000 yuan. Now, the bank manager claims it is 100 yuan, which is a significant discrepancy that needs to be investigated. The court ordered that all transfers of the shares be temporarily prohibited, and that the matter be reviewed after the litigation is completed. When attaching the Xianyi Li property, most of the property was rented to tenants. To avoid disturbing the tenants, the doors were not sealed. However, regarding the collected rent, the defendant Li Jia's attorney suggested depositing it in the Guohua Bank for safekeeping, while the plaintiff's attorney preferred depositing it in the Shanghai Bank. This matter is still under discussion. As for Li Jia Zheng's personal divorce issue, it will likely be resolved after the property division case is settled.

Street Cleaner Knifes Adulterous Couple 124

▲Shameless Man and Woman's Scandal Exposed

▲Jealous Husband Spies, Burning with Rage

▲Holds Knife and Slashes, Then Surrenders

▲To Be Reviewed After the Man and Woman Recover

Liu Tongdao, a 33-year-old street cleaner from Jiangbei, operates a boat for the French Concession Public Works Department, transporting garbage to a wasteland near Gaochangmiao for disposal. He lives with his family in a boat covered with straw mats by the Suzhou Creek. He married Liu Mao, the daughter of Mao Zhou, from his hometown last June 26. Mao, in her early twenties, is attractive but frivolous and immoral. Her husband, Liu Tongdao, recently discovered that she was having an affair with Chen Youcai, who works on a nearby boat. He warned her that if he caught her again, he would attack her with a kitchen knife. On the evening of the 22nd of this month, Liu suspected something when he did not see Chen go to work, and hired a replacement laborer. He rushed home but before entering, he heard lewd sounds from the room. Peeking through the door, he saw his wife naked with Chen Youcai in bed, making love. He was furious. He wanted to confront them but thought he was no match for them. He waited until 3:30 AM when they were asleep. He grabbed a kitchen knife and slashed them. Chen awoke in pain and grabbed the knife, throwing it in the river. A neighbor, Wang Xu, came to the scene and saw Chen and Mao naked, bleeding from the head. She told them to put on clothes. Mao Zhou, the woman's mother, heard the noise and arrived, advocating for a peaceful resolution without reporting to the authorities. Chen fled. At 8:30 AM, Liu surrendered himself to the Xinzha police station, stating the events. The police ordered his arrest and sent detective Shao Jingfan to investigate. No one was there. Chen Youcai was arrested on Wuzhen Road Bridge. Liu Mao surrendered and was sent to Kuangren Hospital for medical treatment. Both had minor injuries. Yesterday, the police sent Liu to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Court. The police attorney, Wang Yaotang, stated the police are charging Liu with attempted murder under Article 284, paragraph 1, item 2 of the Criminal Code, and charging Chen Youcai and Liu Mao with adultery under Article 256 of the Criminal Code. Chen and Mao are in the hospital for treatment, so they were not present in court. Witness Wang Xu testified. The defendant confessed to knifing the adulterous couple. Judge Wu Tingqi ordered Liu Tongdao to post bail. He will be summoned when Chen Youcai and Liu Mao recover.

Number 55, Molier Road, French Concession, along the road, was formerly the residence of an Englishman, Bian Lao, an employee of the Qian Shun Foreign Firm at Number 30, Beijing Road, Public Concession. ▲Believes it Insults Women

▲Writes to Wu and Guo, Resigning as Judges

The National News Agency reported that the Shanghai Women's Relief Association held its seventh preparatory committee meeting yesterday. Attendees included Zhang Xuefei, Bao Guangyu, Lin Kecong, and Wang Xiaoying, with Jin Shiyin attending as an observer. Lin Kecong chaired and Jin Shiyin recorded the minutes. After the chairman and various departments reported, the discussion began. Here are the key resolutions: (1) The case of creating membership badges for the association: (Resolution) Comrade Bao Guangyu is responsible for handling this. (2) The case of how to stop Chinese women from participating in the Beauty Pageant, which insults women: (Resolution) (1) Petition the Social Affairs Bureau to stop Chinese women from joining the Beauty Pageant. (2) The association will write a sister's letter. (3) Send a letter to the two Chinese female judges of the Beauty Pageant. (3) The City Representative Assembly resolved to establish the City Women's Relief Home, but this has not yet been implemented. Should it be urged? (Resolution)

Submit a request to the City Party Department to forward to the Municipal Government, and quickly establish the Shanghai Women's Relief Home in accordance with the City Representative Assembly's resolution. (4) The case of requesting the City Party Department to allocate preparatory funds: (Resolution) Push Wang Xiaoying and Lin Kecong to personally request the City Party Department again. (5) (Omitted) (6) The association previously scheduled the establishment meeting to be held on August 8th at the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Group. Should the allocation of staff be requested?

(Resolution) Nominate Wang Xiaoying, Lin Kecong, and Tang Naixin as the presidium of the meeting, Jin Shiyin as the recorder, Zhang Xuefei as the master of ceremonies, Bao Guangyu and Huang Daping as the secretaries, and Jin Ruyu, Wang Wenzhao, Wang Yazhi, etc. as the hosts. (7) Confirm the establishment dates of the district branches: (Resolution) All must be established before August 1st. The meeting adjourned. The text of the letter from the association to the Social Affairs Bureau and the letter to the two female judges Wu and Guo (the letter to the sisters is slightly longer, so it is omitted) are recorded separately as follows:

▲Letter to the Social Affairs Bureau: Regarding submitting a request to find a way to stop Chinese women from participating in the International Beauty Pageant in order to maintain social morality and respect women's personality, the International Beauty Pageant, nominally competing for beauty, is actually a disguised form of obscenity, using women's flesh for public appreciation, insulting personality like never before. Under our revolutionary government, how can we tolerate such shameless people acting recklessly? Moreover, this matter concerns social morality and the personality of the entire world. If we do not prohibit it, the danger of society's future will be even more unthinkable, and it will contradict the intentions of our leader's revolution. Therefore, we submit this document to request your bureau to find a way to stop Chinese women from participating in the meeting. We sincerely hope that you will review and implement it for the public convenience. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Shanghai Women's Relief Association.

▲Letter to the Judges: It is said that people despise themselves before others despise them. Now is the time for the Party and the country to promote women's rights, and it is the time for our women to encourage and uplift themselves. Unless one is utterly foolish, one would never want to be the culprit. Only the insane would dare to harm the flock. This International Beauty Pageant uses women's flesh as a target for public appreciation, insulting women like never before. All our compatriots should rise up in opposition and unanimously condemn it. We have always admired your enthusiasm for society and your tireless efforts to protect your compatriots. We trust that you will put the honor and disgrace of all women first and hope that you will resign from your positions as judges of the Beauty Pageant as soon as possible, so as not to invite self-despisal and leave a shame on the women's community. This would be our greatest honor. Respectfully to Ms. Wu Ai Yun and Ms. Guo Anci, Shanghai Women's Relief Association.

Trial Opens in Jealousy Murder Case 135

Zhao Du's, a woman from No. 23 Shengzhi Lane, Zixia Road, Dadongmen, although aging, still retained her charm. She became acquainted with Zhao Qilang and Kong Chengrong from Haimen, leading to a jealous conflict. On June 14th, Kong Chengrong was lured to a railway siding in Xiaoshadu and murdered. He was stabbed multiple times, and his genitals were also cut off. The case was widely reported in the newspapers. Zhao Du's son, Zhao Jinrong, informed the police in a letter, leading to the arrest of Zhao Qilang and his accomplice Wang Cailang. They were sent to the District Court, where Prosecutor Yang charged them with murder. Yesterday, Judge Shen presided over the trial. Zhao Qilang testified that he was 34 years old, from Haimen, and lived on Zixia Road, working as a cook. He said that he divorced his wife, and he became intimate with Zhao Du's this January. In February, he was beaten out of her bed by her son, Zhao Jinrong. She then became intimate with Kong Chengrong. On June 14th, he did not call Kong to go out. The official asked if he told Zhao Du's that if asked too many questions, he would kill her along with her. He denied saying that. He also denied knowing Wang Cailang. Wang Cailang testified that he was 28 years old, from Haimen, lived at Haichao Temple, and worked as a cook. He denied knowing Zhao Qilang. He also denied knowing Wang Rongchun. The official asked if he had previously testified that Wang Rongchun told him that Wang, Zhang Zhaoshou, Huang Zhidao, Shi Shuangqing, and others committed the murder. He replied that he had not said that, and that Wang Rongchun only said that he was going to Xiaoshadu. Zhao Du's testified that she was 42 years old, from Changzhou, and that her husband died last June. Zhao Jinrong was her son from her late husband. She said that she became intimate with Zhao Qilang on January 20th, but her son chased him out on March 16th. Later, someone told her that Kong Chengrong had just died and that she could rely on him for the rest of her life, and they started a relationship in early April, staying at inns. On April 29th, she went to Kong's house on Miezuo Street, and Zhao Qilang also came, calling Kong to go to Xiaonanmen. She then went home. The next day, when he did not return, she went to find Zhao Qilang, but he was nowhere to be found. On May 2nd, she met him at Dadongmen, and he said that Kong had gone home. She followed him to look for him, but he said that he would go the next day, going out around 1:00. Unexpectedly, he left first. His landlord told her to go to Huiding Hospital, but she could not find him anywhere. She returned and grabbed Zhao at the Dafang Hotel. He threatened to kill her if she kept bothering him. Later, he told her that the police would be coming soon. After she returned home, she went to Kong's house, and his landlord told her that the newspapers reported that he was dead. Zhao Jinrong testified that he was 29 years old, from Shanghai, and worked in printing. Zhao Du's was his stepmother. After she was driven out for being intimate with Zhao Qilang, he did not know how Kong Chengrong was dating her, nor how he died. On May 5th, he reported the case in a letter because he was in danger. Kong Er'a testified that he was 41 years old, from Haiyan, and lived on Meibike Road. Kong Chengrong was his cousin. He said that he saw a report on the 16th about a male corpse being murdered in Xiaoshadu, and it looked similar to his cousin, so he went to inquire. Afterwards, he could not find Zhao Dalang. He then reported Zhao to First District Police. His wife claimed that Zhao Qilang was the one who murdered her husband. Zhang Zhu's testified that she was 41 years old, from Shanghai, and lived on Miezuo Street. Kong Chengrong was her tenant. She recognized Zhao Qilang because of a mole on his neck. After dinner on April 29, he and Kong Chengrong went out with another person, and he never returned. On the third day of the month, she saw the news report saying that he had been murdered. Hu A'tao testified that she was 57 years old, from Chuansha, and lived near Kong Chengrong. On April 29, she saw Zhao Qilang and Kong Chengrong leave together, and Kong never came back, and Zhao never came back either. Yang Zhuqing testified that he was 38 years old, from Chongming, and Zhao Qilang was his brother-in-law. He did not know how Zhao Qilang was captured after he was arrested by the First District Police. Considering further investigation was needed, the official adjourned the trial. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Verdict in Smuggling Case 139

▲Truck Driver Sentenced to Three and a Half Years

▲Additional Fine of Five Thousand Yuan

Du Chaozhuan, a Tongzhou native working as a driver for Cai Guiji Trucking Company at No. 16 Yihe Lane, Huaji Road, was arrested on the 17th of this month at 1:40 AM while loading 24 bags of opium, weighing 2,088 pounds, at the Gonghexiang Wharf on Zhaofeng Road, for transportation elsewhere. He was stopped by Indian constables No. 617 and No. 644 from the Huishan Police Station. He failed to stop and an officer opened fire, wounding Du in the hand and killing Yu Jinsheng, a Wuxi native who was guarding the goods. It was revealed that a fugitive opium trafficker had bribed the two Indian constables ten dollars. Chinese detective Xu Yongyuan and Western detective Blake took Du and the opium to the Special District Court for questioning and detention. This was already detailed in the newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefen continued the hearing in the Third Court. The police station's lawyer, Li Zhishan, stated that the principal offenders and accomplices could not be apprehended during the postponement. However, the defendant driver had been driving the whole time. The position and bloodstains of the deceased Yu Jinsheng were not in the driver's area. The truck's gas tank was damaged by bullets, causing it to stop. Otherwise, the defendant would have continued to drive away. The deceased was a newly trained apprentice, who specialized in wandering around Huaji Road. Detective Xu stated that at the time, two ships were docked at the wharf, Fuxing and Guangyao Maru, but Fuxing was far from the wharf, while Guangyao Maru was much closer. He investigated the ship, and the crew members claimed they did not know anything. The defendant's testimony was the same as in the previous hearing. After reviewing the statements, Judge Xiao sentenced Du Chaozhuan to three years and six months in prison for aiding and abetting the transportation of opium, and imposed a fine of 5,000 yuan. If the fine is not paid after compulsory execution, it will be converted to imprisonment based on the total amount of the fine divided by the number of days in a year. The number of days spent in custody before the judgment is determined will be credited against the prison term at a rate of two days for each day of imprisonment. The 2,088 pounds of opium and the truck were confiscated. The ten dollars bribe was temporarily placed in storage.

Innovation of Kodak Magazine 140

▲Increase in Pages and Launch of Photography Monthly Competition

Kodak Magazine is one of the leading photography research publications in the country, published monthly without interruption. With its novel content and beautiful copperplate illustrations, it is highly popular with readers and widely circulated. The editors of the magazine are not complacent. Starting with the August issue, there will be major changes and a completely new look. Four pages will be added to provide more research articles on photography, and a new travelogue section will be added, published regularly to provide readers with armchair travel experiences. To encourage reader interest, a monthly photography competition will be launched, offering cash prizes to those with outstanding achievements. All subscribers are welcome to participate in the competition. There is also a Q&A section that is popular with readers. If you have any difficult problems on the art of photography, you can write to inquire at any time, and it will be published in the next issue of the magazine, providing clear answers, and all difficulties will be easily resolved. The August issue will be published soon, with content including The Joys of Water Towns, Famous Sites in Yanjing, Trees, The Value of Landscapes, Large Photos, A Page for Beginners, The Causes of Halos, Micro-Themes for the Photography Monthly Competition, Q&A, Snippets, etc. The material is rich and beautiful. The annual subscription fee is extremely low, only eight dimes (洋角), including postage. Real Estate Association Notice: Renters Must Provide Bond 143

The Shanghai Real Estate Association yesterday sent a letter to its members stating, "We are writing to inform you that the Youcheng Company leased a house at No. 401 Wuding Road to someone who turned out to be a kidnapper. Although a bond was obtained from the tenant at the time, it was returned to him after he moved out, according to customary practice. The court of first instance did not pay attention to this point and, at the request of the police lawyer, ordered the house to be confiscated. The party concerned refused to accept this and filed an appeal. At the request of the party concerned, the Association legally proved the matter to the court of second instance. The appellate court has now ruled that the house be returned. A copy of the judgment is enclosed for reference. From this case, it can be seen that landlords should obtain a bond from tenants as a matter of prudence. If there had been no bond obtained in this case, the landlord would have suffered the disaster of having his property confiscated, regardless of whether he was aware of the tenant's activities or not. This is a notice to be followed and obeyed."

Flood Disaster Reports from Various Provinces 145

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association received a continuous stream of letters and telegrams from various provinces requesting flood relief. Here are excerpts: (Jiangsu) Jiangdu County has been experiencing continuous summer rains this year, almost like the Milky Way pouring down. In addition, the lake waters have risen, and the embankments have collapsed, causing the low-lying areas to become a country of swamps and a vast expanse of water. The crops and houses are all in the water. Tens of thousands of refugees have lost their homes and are wandering around, exposed and crying out for food. We beg for assistance. (Anhui) Fengtai County has been suffering from disasters for years, and the people have no means of living. Last month, the Huai and Fei rivers suddenly rose, breaking through embankments and dams, leading to the deaths of people. Recently, there has been continuous heavy rain for days, and mountain floods have broken through dams. There is no dry land outside of Doucheng. Houses have been washed away, and people and animals have been swept away. There is nothing but water as far as the eye can see. No fewer than ten thousand disaster victims are without firewood and rice, crying out for food. Please provide relief quickly. Fengtai County Chamber of Commerce, etc. Secondly, Shouxian County had a poor harvest of early wheat, and recently has been ravaged by continuous rain. Mountain floods have broken out, flooding fields and houses, killing countless people and animals. The situation is extremely tragic. Please provide aid to benefit the disaster victims. The Shouxian branch of the Anhui Red Cross Society. Secondly, the Fuyang Red Swastika Society telegraphed that Fuyang was unfortunate, and disasters occurred frequently. There was a major flood last month, coupled with heavy rain that did not stop day and night. In addition, mountain floods broke out upstream, flooding the ground and flowing horizontally. Cities, towns, and villages are a country of water. Innumerable people and animals have been drowned. Houses have collapsed, and crops have been flooded. Millions of disaster victims have no place to escape, and their livelihood has been broken. Secondly, the Huoqiu Chamber of Commerce sent a quick letter stating that Huoqiu had continuous cloudy and rainy weather during the Little Full solar term of this year, and mountain floods broke out, making the areas along the bayous become a country of swamps. Wheat was flooded, and the people were out of food. Before the previous flood receded, heavy rain began on July 2, like mountains falling and seas pouring. It lasted for several days and nights, causing the water to be several feet deep on the plains, and the water was even more intense in the towns. Fields and houses were completely washed away, and innumerable people and animals were drowned, even entire families were destroyed. At the moment, the fog is still diffuse and there is no sunlight. The fields are barren, the wells and villages are in ruins, food is running out, and there is no place to live. There are hundreds of holes and thousands of sores, and there is no way to heal them. Please provide relief. Secondly, the Inland Mission Gospel Church of Sanhejian, northern Anhui, sent a letter stating that there were heavy rains for three days and nights last month, and the water was more than one or ten feet deep on the plains, and countless embankments were broken, and many people and animals were drowned. The victims are living in the open air, their livelihoods are cut off, and they are waiting for assistance. Secondly, the Five River County Flood Relief Association requested assistance, stating that on the eleventh of this month, there was a torrential rain that caused the Hui River to overflow and compete with the Huai River, both flowing into the Five Rivers, and the high embankments along the Huai River and the dams downstream were all overflowing with water. Innumerable people, animals, houses, goods, and fields were drowned and destroyed. The disaster victims are now living in the open air and exposed to the wind, lacking both food and shelter. Please provide prompt relief. Secondly, the Ying Shang County groups came to beg for relief, saying that in the early ten days of July, there was a sudden downpour and flood broke out, overflowing the river and making the plains seem endless. Countless people, animals, houses, and fields were washed away. The disaster victims' food and shelter are all lost, and they are crying out for food, not knowing if they can survive tomorrow. Please allocate funds for relief. Secondly, the Ying Shang Red Swastika Society telegraphed the disaster situation, which was the same as before. (Henan) The Ye County Red Cross Society sent a letter requesting assistance, stating that on June 28, there was a heavy rain for three days and nights, and the Kun and Xun rivers broke out at the same time, causing the country to be filled with water. Thousands of acres of fertile land were turned into swamps. Recently, there have been heavy rains again for several days, and the river is even larger. Innumerable people and animals have been washed away, and the victims are waiting for assistance. Secondly, Zhang Fang, from Kaifeng, telegraphed, reporting continuous rains for a month, and a flood broke out. All counties in eastern, western, and northern Henan were affected by the flood. The fields and crops were completely destroyed, and there were refugees everywhere. Innumerable people and animals were washed away. At present, the people are waiting for assistance, and it is urgent. Please provide assistance. (Guangdong) A telegram stated that in this flood, the landslides in Lianzhou flowed directly downstream, and the area was wide and the disaster was deep. We are now launching an emergency relief effort and uniting all sectors of society to establish a relief association. Please assist with the donation of funds. It is said that the association is extremely anxious due to the wide scope of the disaster and the lack of funds.

Anhui Native Association Telegram Urges Emergency Relief for Floods 146

The Anhui Native Association sent a telegram to the central government, "To Chairman Jiang of the Nanjing National Government and Chairman Xu of the Relief Committee: We have received reports from various counties along the river and Huai River in this province. The sky has sent continuous rain, and the rivers Huai have flooded. Embankments have collapsed, and floods have overflowed. The wheat season was not fully harvested, and the autumn harvest is now hopeless. The disaster victims are more than tens of millions. In particular, the counties along the Huai River are most severely affected, more than three feet higher than the two major floods in Jiyou, 1929 and 1930. Huge waves were raging and the sky was boundless. Places like Fuyang, Huoqiu, Shouxian, Ying Shang, Woyang, Mengcheng, Taihe, Bo County, Wuhe, Huaiyuan, Dingyuan, Fengtai, Tianchang, Xuyi, Sixian, Su County, Lingbi, Fengyang, and Quanjiao were reported to have losses of 90 percent or more of houses and land and innumerable people drowned. The survivors climbed to the tops of trees and roofs, without food, and were swept away by the wind and waves, joining the sea. The bodies of people and animals floated down the river and could not be salvaged and buried. Farm implements and utensils were drifting in the water, and firewood, grass, and rice were all washed away. Even more than 300 refugees in Huoqiu, who were escaping the bandits, were washed away by the water overnight at Sanhe and their fate is unknown. A family of seven surnamed Cao in Fengtai knew there was no way to live, so they tied themselves together with ropes and went with the waves. Shouxian City was like the bottom of a pot, with water inundating the city walls, and the whole city was in danger of collapsing. Zhengyang, Huaiyuan, and other cities, and Bengbu, Linhuai, Luqiao, and Mingguang and all of the towns were submerged in water. Telephone poles were broken, ships were stopped, and transportation was cut off, and news was not coming. The tragic situation cannot be described. Even if the water recedes, the autumn planting will be delayed and homes will be destroyed, and there will be no way to live. Please provide relief. Read the letters begging for relief from each county, and each word is a tear. We cannot bear to read them. This flood is a catastrophe of unprecedented scale. In an instant, the country was turned into a swamp. Flesh and blood were separated, and the land was turned into ruins. The dead cannot be buried, and the epidemics after autumn are fearful. The living have no place to live, and their pots are broken, and there is no smoke from their stoves. Compared with any other disaster, there is nothing so tragic. We respectfully request that you will quickly issue national currency for immediate relief and prepare for a Huai River irrigation project to prevent displacement. We hope to alleviate the urgency of the water and quickly order the provincial government to rush to repair the dikes along the river to avoid collapse. We plead for the suffering people of the province.” The Anhui Native Association in Shanghai bowed and respectfully requested.

Universal Benevolence Villa Manages Burial of the Exposed in Jiangsu and Zhejiang 148

Mr. Wang Junsheng, Director of the Universal Benevolence Villa, has been entrusted by Mr. Wang Yiting, Chairman of the United Charity Organizations, to manage the burial of the exposed corpses in the Jiangsu-Zhejiang border area since four years ago. Investigations in various locations have revealed a total of over 160,000 corpses, a truly unbearable sight. Although 46,835 bodies have been buried, three-quarters remain unburied. Recently, Director Wang personally went to the inland areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang at his own expense to connect with prominent county magistrates and righteous gentry to gradually carry out the work. He plans to resume operations as early as this autumn. The required expenses are estimated to be over 10,000 yuan. Mr. Wang Yiting, deeply concerned about the large number of exposed and unburied corpses, has generously allocated 3,832 yuan from the celebrations for his father and mother's 90th birthday to support the expenses. The remaining amount still needs to be urgently raised. It is believed that this benevolent act of burial can eliminate the uncivilized custom of not burying the dead in the inland areas and will greatly benefit local public health. It is hoped that kind-hearted people from all walks of life will make benevolent vows and generously contribute to achieve complete success and improve sanitation. The merit of this undertaking is truly significant.

Customs Brokerage Industry Requests the Cancellation of Japanese Merchants' Customs Brokerage Firms 149

The Shanghai Transshipment and Customs Brokerage Association sent letters to the City Party Headquarters, the City Chamber of Commerce, and the Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Association yesterday, stating: We respectfully report that before the settlement of the ten-thousand case dispute, the disaster of overseas Chinese in the Three Han (Korea) has already arrived. All of our countrymen share a deep sense of indignation. How can our industry sit idly by? Since the previous boycotts, the Japanese have been deliberately plotting. They know that the customs brokerage industry is fundamental to strangling Japanese goods. Japanese merchants in this city have been secretly organizing similar businesses, hoping to achieve a position of self-declaration and self-loading. Our industry has long been squeezed out of the market for goods going to the northern Yangtze River area. If we do not take action against Japanese customs brokerage firms according to international private law while discussing the severance of relations with Japan, it would be like chasing fish into a deep pool or scaring sparrows into a thicket. A large portion of Japanese goods will be handled and transported by the Japanese themselves. Although we in the industry are determined to save the country, we lack the means to do so. Therefore, we must inform your association in detail. When our industry clears customs, such as cotton yarn shipped to Dalian, we charge customers two taels and three qian per piece for dockage and other fees. However, the Japanese rely on factory support and enjoy various advantages, so they lower the price to one tael and six qian. It is already difficult to compete with this situation. Once relations with Japan are severed, the Japanese will certainly use all their tricks to collude with treacherous merchants and flaunt the convenience of self-declaration and self-loading, determined to attract business by lowering prices. Domestic treacherous merchants will inevitably fall for their tricks. The difficulty of this boycott will exceed that of the previous ones. We urge your association to find a way to address this. In advanced countries, foreigners are absolutely not allowed to operate customs brokerage businesses. The influence of China's tariff agreements has allowed the Japanese to freely clear customs, resulting in a loss of national sovereignty, which is undeniable. Even if the ten-thousand case dispute had not occurred, we should call on the authorities to immediately ban this. Now is the time for our country to strive for self-salvation and self-preservation. Therefore, we respectfully submit our situation and urge you to forward it to the Ministry of Finance, ordering the Tax Affairs Department to issue a document to the Customs, citing international private law to revoke the licenses of all Japanese customs brokerage firms. This will uphold national sovereignty, take into account commercial transport, and greatly benefit the national economy and the people's livelihood. The future of the boycott will be unimpeded. We eagerly await your instructions.

▲Informal Meeting Held the Day Before Yesterday

▲Sharing of Internal Responsibilities

Zhao Zhizhi and three other members of the Chinese Seamen's Industrial Joint Federation, along with Secretary Liu Yuzhou, left their positions the month before last, taking away important seals. Afterwards, three members, Miao Shuizhang, Qiu Yaokui, and Mu Yeyi, reported to the central authorities and requested instructions. The union affairs were temporarily maintained by the three members. Later, Zhang Jianbai was appointed by the central authorities, and He Zhenhuan, Ma Zhongxian, Wang Yongsheng, and others from the Shanghai branch were promoted. At the same time, eleven articles of the organizational law were promulgated, and the name was changed to the Chinese Seamen's Union Reorganization Committee. Under the three departments of general affairs, guidance, and investigation, it is said that six sections will be established: arbitration, accounting, organization, statistics, investigation, and documentation. Internal organization has been discussed for several days, and is actively progressing. As soon as the official seal is issued, they will take office and begin work. Secretary Wu, who was appointed by the central authorities, has also arrived in Shanghai and will officially begin work soon. Since He and Ma were promoted to members of the general association, the Shanghai branch has suspended its regular meetings on Tuesdays and Fridays due to insufficient members. Committee Member Tang previously reported to the central authorities for instructions, but no reply has been received. However, the union affairs are being handled by Tang and Luo.

New News from the Art World 154

▲Summer, Xu, Huang Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition. Xia Anjingguan, Xu Shaozhouzhenli, and Huang Gongzhuxiaoshu, the three gentlemen, are all known for their literary achievements. Their poems, lyrics, parallel prose, and essays are all exquisite. They once formed the Ou Society in Shanghai with Zhu Qiangcun, Ye Xiaan, Pan Lanshi, Zhou Mengpo, Yuan Bokui, Wang Xishen, Zhao Shuyong, Wu Hufan, Lin Ziyou, Chen Yantong, and others. The society is named after "Ou," taken from Mr. Qiangcun's alias "Ou Yin." The three gentlemen are also skilled in the six principles of painting, striving to emulate the lofty and profound styles of the Song and Yuan dynasties, avoiding seductive charm, and their artistic spirit is high. The residence of Xia An is located at Kangjiaqiao on Route Extreme and is a scenic garden with excellent flowers and trees. Xu and Huang have visited Cambridge and, during their leisure time, have created many works together. Therefore, from the 24th to the 26th of this month, an exhibition will be held at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association on Xizang Road for three days. Robbery of Railway Foreman 159

At around 6:30 PM on Wednesday of this week, ten robbers, seven of whom were armed with pistols, broke into the home of Zhen Yousan, the foreman of the Maigen Road construction site of the Zhabei-Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, and robbed him of 70 silver yuan, 500 paper yuan, four gold rings, one gold bracelet, and miscellaneous gold ornaments and clothing. The victim reported the incident to the railway police and the Tanzhiwan police station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau and requested an investigation. According to Zhen's wife, Ms. Liu, when the robbers went to commit the robbery, her husband had gone out to buy things. They lived in one room on the east side of the construction site, and nine workers lived in the three rooms on the west side. At the time of the incident, five people had already fallen asleep, and the remaining four had gone out and not returned.

Tragic Death of a Fourteen-Year-Old Child 160

Lu Shunbao, a fourteen-year-old child from Jiangsu, was walking through the intersection of Edward Road and Fujian Road yesterday morning at around 9:00 AM when he was suddenly hit by a car with the number 6415 speeding by. He was unable to avoid it and was crushed under the wheels, injuring his head. The patrol officer number 3256 from the Lao Zha Station arrived, recorded the car number, and carried the injured child to Renji Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died at around 2:00 PM. The hospital transferred the body to the morgue for examination, pending a report to the court for inspection.

Decision: Send a letter to correct it. Other cases were omitted.

A Word of Observation 169

— Yi Mei

▲Nothing can match the intelligence of humans. Nothing can also match the violence of humans.

▲Most modern women are incarnations of Rakshasas.

▲Writers who rack their brains in the summer suffer no less than laborers who run in the hot sun.

▲Eyebrows fly without wings, and colors dance without joy.

Solemn and Enthusiastic Memorial Service for Overseas Chinese 170

— Sun Choucheng

On the morning of the 23rd of this month, people from all walks of life in Shanghai held a memorial service at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce for the overseas Chinese who died in Korea. Many people attended, and the atmosphere was very solemn. On that day, the Kuomintang flag and the national flag were crossed at the entrance of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, with a bamboo cloth banner hanging in the middle. The banner read: "Shanghai All Circles Memorial Service for Overseas Chinese Killed in Korea." Due to the wind and rain, the cloth was soaked, and the red color on the flag stained the cloth, dripping down like blood and tears, which was moving. The venue was in the conference hall. A registration desk was set up at the entrance, and representatives from all walks of life were given black yarn to wear on their arms after registering. The Shanghai Korean Groups United Association deeply hated the Japanese use of ignorant Koreans as puppets in this incident. In order to show their determination, they distributed leaflets on the spot entitled "A Letter to the Chinese People," detailing the Japanese premeditation and sinister means against China. Please note that after the fall of Korea, the Japanese oppression was extremely severe. Even the elementary school send-off meetings and the annual parent-teacher meetings were prohibited. How could the Japanese claim they were unable to suppress the thousands of Koreans who gathered for seven or eight days of slaughter? It also published six slogans: "Consolidate the Hua-Han Joint Front," "Unite to Support Revolutionary Diplomacy," "Uphold China's Sovereignty over Manchuria and Mongolia," "Long Live Korean Independence," "Long Live the Completion of the Chinese National Revolution," "Down with Japanese Imperialism." On the stage was a white cloth spirit tablet for the deceased overseas Chinese. There were no incense candles or sacrificial dishes. The stage entrance was piled with wreaths, which were donated by the Women's Relief Association. The four walls were covered with memorial banners and elegiac couplets. What I remember is recorded as follows: "Trampling on our country's land, harming our overseas Chinese compatriots, acting fiercely and unprecedentedly. If this is tolerable, what is not tolerable?" "Resist their trade, cut off their economy, persist to the end. Existence lies here, death also lies here." The Timber Industry Association. "The overseas Chinese in the sad chopping block became martyrs." "The Korean people under the mournful iron hooves were made to work for the Japanese." The Embroidery Industry Association. "Sad today, a cavity of hot blood sprays the public enemy." "Sacrifice in a foreign land, ancient heroic souls match the country's calamity." The Book Industry Association. "Cross the sea to the East, merchants, farmers, and workers, diligently operate, can be called honest and upright. Unexpectedly, a tragic robbery occurred. The world was dark. Don't say there is a number of this." "Leave the ancestral home, fathers, brothers, sons and daughters, hard management, only rely on self-reliance. Unexpectedly, a conspiracy broke out. Wolves and pigs suddenly appeared. Who says there is no one behind it." The comrades of the Shanghai Korean Gang. "The Koreans who排華 are instigated by the Japanese. They act arbitrarily, hurting our country's land. Bad news spreads, righteous indignation fills the chest, calling and running, hoping for some punishment. Economic severance, boycott of Japanese goods, work together with one heart, do not slacken. Lie on firewood and taste bitterness, the public will becomes a city, avenge this odd shame, is to comfort the gods." The Shanghai National Goods Factory Union. During the public sacrifice, members of the presidium took turns to read wills, offer flowers, read sacrificial texts, and deliver reply speeches to balance labor and leisure. During the speeches, the representative of the Social Bureau stated that the Northeast region is vast and sparsely populated, making it easy for the Japanese to covet it, and emphasized the need to pay attention to the development of the Northeast. The representative of the Korean community in Shanghai spoke in Chinese, stating that the Japanese used Korean thugs as pawns with sinister means. The representative of the Korean gang cited the fact that the Japanese had prepared in advance. Mrs. Cai Gongshi stated the ferocity of the Japanese. The representative of the City Party Headquarters stated the ambitions of the Japanese. The representative of the women's organization advised people not to buy Japanese goods in this life. The representative of the national goods organization hoped to achieve the goal of paying life for murder. The representative of the labor community emphasized that this anti-Japanese movement must be thorough and lasting. Several people also stood up to express their opinions temporarily. Some urged the committee to handle the boycott of Japanese goods fairly and not be blinded by material desires. Some reported that someone was smuggling Japanese goods on a barge and asked the inspection department to pay attention to the search. Tao Baichuan expressed his acceptance of the opinions and suggestions when giving his reply speech. He was willing to do his best to fight for the country's honor and comfort the overseas Chinese who died underground. The meeting ended when the clock struck twelve. I dip my pen to record this and express my sorrow.

Mr. Feng of Cixi Recounts 172

— Chen Qihuai

Mr. Feng, styled Junmu, originally named Hongchi, styled Jieqing, was a native of Cixi. The Feng family of Cixi was a renowned lineage. Since the beginning of history, there have been people from the family who distinguished themselves through literature in every generation. Mr. Feng's achievements were particularly numerous. In his studies, he attended to the great without neglecting the small. His extensive knowledge and strong memory resembled those of Wang Shenning. His writings were lofty, outstanding, and austere in their purity, inwardly refined and outwardly unrestrained, like those of Wang Rongfu. In his generation, no one could match him. His poetry initially followed the styles of Du Fu and Han Yu, approaching the refinement of Li Shangyin (Yuxi). In middle age, he gradually adopted the style of the Jiangxi School. Later in life, amid turmoil and separation, his reputation diminished. Whenever he composed poems, he would harmonize with a thousand and blend with hundreds of spirits, expressing his emotions. He once said, "Composing poetry should be about finding flavor in the tasteless and seeing talent in the untalented. But who in this world understands this?" Throughout his life, he valued righteousness and upheld principles. In his youth, he and fellow townsmen Chen Jingtang, Zheng Guangzu, Feng Yuzi, Ying Qichi, Qian Baohang, Wei Youfang, Yao Shouqi, and others formed the Dun Society. They established society rules, encouraging each other to do good and admonishing each other for their faults, mutually advancing in learning and moral principles. The group discussed who should lead, and some suggested Mr. Feng. Mr. Feng said that Jingtang was clear, upright, and highly learned, truly beyond the reach of his peers, and thus suitable to be the leader. Later, some in the Dun Society were criticized for flaunting and repeating mistakes. Mr. Feng then proposed renaming it the Yan Society, a gathering for poetry and wine. Yan was chosen because Jingtang resided near Yan Mountain. Mr. Feng judged others critically, rarely praising them. He deeply admired those who were superior to him, holding them in high esteem. People respected him more for this. Mr. Feng showed early promise and quickly gained fame in his hometown. Scholars from all directions visited his courtyard, earnestly seeking his acquaintance or presenting gifts. Mr. Feng sincerely opened his heart to those who came. He would share whatever he knew, and he would never fail to tell what he had heard. He was naturally sensitive and cherished harmony. He treated everyone equally, without regard to distance or closeness. Once he connected with someone, he remained loyal for life. In his actions, he never severed ties with the common people and communicated without doubting the present. He was different in temperament from those who were content with themselves. His inner cultivation surpassed others, and his study of antiquity was marked by innovation. In his later years, he lectured in Shanghai, frequently interacting with renowned scholars of the previous dynasty. Wu Changshuo of Anji, Kuang Zhouyi of Lingui, and Zhu Xiaozang of Wuxing were particularly close to him. Several years before his death, Wu Changshuo left instructions that Mr. Feng should write his epitaph. He had just begun drafting it when he fell ill. After three months of illness, he passed away at the age of fifty-nine. Alas, heaven has deprived us of this literary talent, and the nation is without such a person. How lamentable! Mr. Feng's father, whose name is unknown, studied Confucianism without success and chose to live as a recluse in the city. He excelled at painting, and his calligraphy was elegant and refined. His mother, née Yu, was the daughter of a local Confucian scholar. She was knowledgeable, courteous, and skilled at educating her children. Mr. Feng lost his father at a young age and relied on his mother to learn poetry, grow up, become independent, and achieve success. At the age of twenty-eight, he became an instructor in Lishui County after passing the selection process for tribute students. He authored several volumes of the "Huifengtang Poetry and Prose Collection," one volume of "Lyrics," several volumes of "Diaries," and various other works. He married a woman surnamed Yu, named Yin, who authored one volume of "Fuxuezhai Lyrics." He later married women surnamed Chen and Li. He had two sons: Zhenxu, born to Yu, and Zhenyong, born to Li. He had one daughter: Zhenyu, born to Li. He had one grandson: Zhaosui, and one granddaughter: Zhaoduo, children of Zhenxu.

▲Brief News: Liang Junzong Ding, the current factory director of the Northeast Mining Bureau, is committed to improving industry and promoting domestic goods. His younger brother, Mr. Diancheng, is skilled in chemistry and enjoys research. He and Mr. Chen Zhenyan, the former magistrate of Taixian County who emphasized practical industries, jointly established the Sanhe Pickles Company in Lion Lane, Yangzhou. He serves as the manager and hires skilled workers to produce Sanfu Autumn Oil and Ten-Scenery Pickles using scientific methods. Because the company was founded by three people, they use "Sanhe" as their trademark. Their products include dozens of varieties such as earth lotus root, pickled bamboo shoots, milky melon, and candied ginger, packaged in cans to last for a long time. Each can costs just over twenty cents, which is much cheaper than the one-dollar-per-can "Fukushima Pickles" (also pickles) sold on the market. Not only is the taste better, but the price is also much lower. During this period of economic boycott against Japan, it is appropriate to vigorously promote this. It is reported that in Shanghai, the Jinghuatang Pharmacy manager in North Xinxinqiao and other major companies and various Southern goods stores are selling them. (Prepared)

Travelogue of India (68) 173

— Linghua

Along the Ganges River bank, there are many men and women living there. There are fewer female ascetics; naturally, there are more men. They vary from poor to rich, but there are more poor people. There are ancient stone piles, intact like temples, that have collapsed on the shore. It is said that they were washed down by the great flood of the past. Many new temples are being built in the future. There is a large flower pool with very clean water. It must be a great baptismal site. It makes one think that from the Ganges to the Jordan River, this ten-thousand-mile religious area is not far apart. The ancient sages all washed their hearts with water and were saved. There are ascetics who are naked and facing the sun, with only a rope tied around their waists and between their thighs. There are ascetics whose hair hangs down a foot. There are ascetics whose whole bodies are covered with ash, sitting quietly without speaking. In short, if one takes spirit as religion, then Indian culture is the world's teacher. If one takes material things as religion, then America is the king of the present age. If one takes the overthrow of material things as religion, then Russia is the king of the world. But if one takes the great mean, righteousness, fairness, and civilization as religion, perhaps the whole world will rely on China. I observe the arduous cultivation of Indian high scholars, and it makes me yearn for the ancient sages' techniques of self-salvation and saving the world.

A student told me, "Benares is a holy land in all of India. There are many university professors and doctors who still wish to die on the banks of the Ganges in Benares." I was shocked and asked the reason. "Are they committing suicide by throwing themselves into the river?" He said, "No. It is because all Indians have long believed that the holy land of Benares is close to the gods. Whoever dies here will have their body burned to ashes and thrown into the Ganges and be reborn in heaven." I heard the child's words and was filled with emotion. The child's fleshly body will not remain in the world for long; it is only dust. Therefore, the famous people in our country take being born in heaven as liberation. I am very surprised that this child is expounding the Dharma to me. I believe that the Buddhist scriptures repeatedly record Manjushri teaching other children. The philosophy of life of Indian children is so sharp.

Recently, there have been conflicts between Indians and British police again. Indians committed suicide. It is a common occurrence for Indians to clash with the British, but instead of killing the British, they commit suicide. I asked an Indian about it. The Indian said, "Gandhi teaches us not to resist the British, so we commit suicide. We would rather commit suicide than kill the British, so as not to implicate our families and friends." Indians originally considered suicide to be wrong and quite denied it in religion. Now Gandhi does not teach resistance to the British, so many are angry and commit suicide. Their resentment towards the British is great. There will definitely be an outbreak one day.

As for boycotting British goods, Indians say that they can save 60,000,000 yuan a year. Therefore, the whole country is united, unlike our country, where the boycott of foreign goods only lasts for five minutes. The streets are full of people wearing our country's style of coarse cloth mourning caps. Even wealthy families use coarse cloth as tablecloths. Gandhi's teachings are very similar to Lao Tzu's revivalist school: sweeten their food, beautify their clothing, delight in their dwellings, and have no contact with each other until they die. They resist material things with extreme spirit, and the materialist school has a tendency to fail. But then, can spirit also be feared? A professor told me that he observed Russian statistics. Since the establishment of the Russian government, the percentage of people receiving education has reached over 20%, compared to only 3% in old Russia. To this day, the average education in India is only 3% to 6%. In short, some Indians are inclined towards Gandhi, and some new factions are inclined towards Russia. There are also those who are inclined towards China. Their progress is the same. There is truly hope for the future. The great revolutions in China and Russia have all given the Indians great stimulation.

Rotary Club Tales

??? (32) 174

— Xu Zhuodai

Ziliang immediately used two fingers to catch it. He didn't dare to personally execute it, fearing that his hands would smell. So, he placed it on the melting oil on top of the candle, and sure enough, its body stuck fast and it started to burn.

"Since today is your first time practicing, you don't need to catch too many. I'll limit you to three!"

Seeing how easy it was for him, Madam naturally wanted to set a number for him. Little did she know that while the first one was a fluke, the second one turned out to be extremely difficult. He searched for a long time and simply couldn't find one. Finally, he found a young bedbug in the seam of the bedsheet, its body still completely red. He put it on the candle in the same way. The second one was already a big hassle, and the third one was of course even harder. Fortunately, Ziliang was resourceful and found a bedbug shell under the mattress. He used it to pretend to be a bedbug and put it on the candle.

Seeing that the three were complete, Madam made a closing statement:

"Alright! All the bedbugs are caught. We can sleep now!"

Ziliang secretly glanced at his watch and saw that it wasn't even nine o'clock yet. It would be a pity to waste such good time by sleeping so early instead of revising his essay:

"You go to sleep first. I still have things to do."

As soon as Ziliang said that, Madam came back at him:

"You're really unappreciative! I'm taking care of you by only asking you to catch three bedbugs, and after you're done, you don't even come to be with me, and want to go back! Fine! Then you catch thirty for me! You can't do good deeds!"

Before Madam could finish speaking, Ziliang had already taken off his clothes and was planning to go to bed.

Gold Standard Rebounds by Four Taels 175

▲Stormy Waves and Continued Fluctuations: Yesterday, the 24th, the gold standard showed a slight uptrend, with strong fluctuations. Between morning and noon, there was a ten-tael turnover, with stormy waves. The evening market only rose or fell by two or three taels, but eventually rebounded by four taels. It can be said that "a large drop is followed by a small rebound." The psychology of the industry seems to be weakening, but the overall selling pressure persists. From early morning, the silver market showed a decline and then rose. Afterwards, drafts were firm and then loosened, but the gold price was weak and then stabilized, once breaking through the forty-tael mark. The after-market revolved around forty taels, but there were no large-scale transactions, and the fluctuations were not as intense as in the morning market. Later, it remained firm.

▲Interest Rates: (Foreign Coppers) The early market interest rate was slightly better by 1 hao, 2 hu, and .5 than the day before yesterday afternoon, at 7 qian, 2 fen, 4 li, 8 hao, and .75 hu. The afternoon market suddenly rose by 3 hao and .7 hu to 7 qian, 2 fen, 5 li, and .5 hao. As a result, it was half a li better than the day before. (Silver Interest) The early market was 7 fen, and the afternoon market was 8 fen, slightly smaller by one or two fen than the day before. The head subsidy still had a market of 4 or 5 fen. The silver market was generally calm.

▲Subsidiary Coin Market Conditions: Jiangnan small foreign coppers were 6 qian, 4 fen, and 9 li in the early market, and 6 qian and 5 fen in the afternoon market. As a result, they were slightly less by half a li than the day before yesterday. Transactions amounted to 2,500 jiao in the early market and 4,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Guangdong small foreign coppers were 6 qian, 4 fen, and 2 li in the early market, and 6 qian, 4 fen, and 2.375 li in the afternoon market. Transactions amounted to 155,000 jiao in the early market and 110,000 jiao in the afternoon market. Copper coins only increased by 700 wen, totaling 378,700 wen.

▲Inflow and Outflow of Silver and Foreign Coppers (Silver Funds) The bank transactions and payment situation in the market yesterday were still fair and unremarkable. Chinese merchants paid more than 1.9 million in drafts, foreign merchants paid more than 1.67 million in drafts, special funds paid more than 2 million, and various goods, exchange taxes, and miscellaneous funds paid more than 8.56 million. 800,000 was placed in the warehouse and 500,000 was taken out. The Japanese Commercial Bank paid more than 3.4 million in various funds and placed 400,000 in the warehouse. Qianzhuang and silver public offices paid more than 46.6 million in single payments, and the head subsidy funds paid more than 3.4 million. Remittances from various routes paid more than 1.1 million, and cash was paid out for 7-800,000. (Foreign Copper Funds) The early market saw 2.45 million in draft payments, and the afternoon market saw 875,000. Banknotes were 55,000 in the early market and 30,000 in the afternoon market. Off-site banknotes were 142,000 in the early market and 125,000 in the afternoon market. Bank transactions had 1.1 million in mutual transactions in the early market and 630,000 in the afternoon market. The foreign copper accounts of various banks had more than 1.6 million in inflows and outflows, and more than 2.2 million in banknotes. Qianzhuang and foreign public offices paid more than 4.7 million in single payments, and the foreign copper head subsidy funds paid more than 1.7 million. Interbank loans of foreign copper funds had more than 1.5 million in inflows and outflows, and small qianzhuang transactions had more than 600,000.

Securities and Bond Markets Continue to Fall 179

Yesterday's bond market, the futures market was calm. The sentiment of buyers and sellers in the front and rear markets was always idle. The spot transactions were also as sparse as before. The various prices yesterday mostly fell, but the major buyers and sellers all only entered and exited sporadically, so the supply and demand situation was very flat. The prices only circled downwards, without seeing major changes. The stagnant situation was really no different than before. As a result, the February 0 future and the July 0 customs both fell by 1 yuan and 2 jiao. The August 19 customs futures and the current month's entire six copies also fell by 8 or 9 jiao. The others only had ups and downs of several jiao. Observing the current state of the bond market, it seems that it has not yet escaped the depressed state. It is estimated that the spot transactions were only 4,000 yuan, and the futures were only more than 11.6 million. In addition, the Securities Exchange decided to temporarily conduct one trading session in the afternoon starting from today due to the increasingly hot weather.

Cotton Yarn: Yarn Market Fluctuates 180

The yarn market was weak in the morning and rose in the afternoon, with a generally tight trend. Because the inspection of inferior goods was very strict, some people still had strong bullish intentions. However, rumors about the current situation continued to be heard, and the business of 10-count coarse yarn remained sluggish. The empty amount of a certain major household did not move, and both sides were in a stalemate. However, the sales of spot yarn were still developing, and the transactions of Japanese yarn on the market were lonely, while the price of domestic yarn was trending upwards.

▲People's Standard Afternoon Rebound: The exchange's People's Standard opened in the morning with American cotton being flat and each month falling by 7.9 qian to 1 tael. In the afternoon, it was heard that the current sales were good and the trend of inspecting inferior goods was tight, so the market atmosphere suddenly turned tight and bullish, with each month rising by 3.6 qian to 1 tael and 2 qian. The transactions totaled 28,650 bales. It was found that Xincheng sold 1,250 bales, Yuantai 700 bales, Tianlong 700 bales, Rongxing 650 bales, and Jifeng 900 bales. Dachang bought 1,100 bales, Deji 750 bales, Gengfeng 800 bales, and Shenchang 600 bales.
