Cotton Market Lacks Progress 181

The cotton market trend shows slight fluctuations. Due to the mediocre performance of foreign cotton and the poor weather in this port—intermittent rain and sunshine—concerns arise about the development of new cotton. Some areas report water damage. Therefore, inland merchants tend to buy, while the local brokers are slightly selling. Current cotton business remains sluggish.

▲Hanbiao Initially Drops, Then Rises The Hanbiao market on the exchange opened lower due to flat foreign cotton and sunny weather, dropping three to four cents. In the afternoon, it became overcast, and the weather tightened, rising three cents. Total transaction volume was 100,080 bales. Sales included 3,400 bales of Jifeng, 2,000 bales of Shenchang, 2,000 bales of Yichang, and 2,500 bales of Jinfeng. Grain: River Rice Market Sales Brisk, Prices Rising 183

▲Xinzha: Yesterday, slightly fewer goods arrived from the west. Heavy rain in the morning prevented any buying. By the afternoon, the weather cleared, and shops facing the market were quite active. Recently, there has been too much rain, causing anxiety. River rice reserves are dwindling, and fewer new arrivals are seen. Prices are gradually increasing, with Changsu thick japonica rice and early/late rice harvests arriving in small quantities. Prices are 3 to 6 jiao higher than the previous two days. Kunshan rice and Luyang pointed rice are both up 2 to 3 jiao, and the trend is tightening. Glutinous rice fluctuates slightly. The river factories sold 5,000 to 6,000 dan of various goods.

▲Nanshi: Due to the rain, few goods arrived from various sources. River reserves are also low. City and rural shops sold well due to the rain, making it difficult to ship goods from the interior, boosting confidence. Shops were active in buying, leading to high transaction volumes. The price of thick japonica rice increased by another 2 to 3 jiao. Thin rice arrivals are lacking, but demand is high. The market price increased by about 2 jiao. Until 10 o'clock, only two boats arrived, but they had not yet started selling. The arrival of thin and thick japonica rice is increasingly rare. It is heard that there has been too much rain in various places for days, and low-lying areas may be flooded. Duyang pointed rice is still available in small quantities and sells well. Prices have increased, and supply and demand are tight, creating a firm market.

Flour Market's Buying Interest Is Strong 184

▲Inland Merchants Compete to Buy Regardless of Price

Yesterday, the flour market showed a firm and brisk trend. Although the quoted price of foreign wheat decreased slightly by 1 to 2 jiao, from the previous day to yesterday morning, there were torrential downpours, no different from a deluge. Disaster reports frequently came from Jiangnan and Jiangbei, and food prices rose sharply. Therefore, inland merchants and those along the Yangtze River spared no effort to compete for purchases regardless of market prices (with half-day transactions reaching over 1.1 million). Fortunately, some factories had fixed production, so they sold forward contracts, and the market atmosphere gradually stabilized. Otherwise, the increase would have been even more considerable. Looking ahead, due to the rain, it is feared that public sentiment will not easily calm down. As a result, this month increased by 1.5 fen compared to Wednesday, August increased by 1 fen, September, October, and November increased by 7.5 li, and December increased by 2.5 li.

Wheat Futures' Rising Trend Is Formidable 185

▲Inland Merchants and Factories Absorb 200 to 300 Cars

Yesterday, the wheat futures market showed a serious trend. People in the interior generally believed that the continuous heavy rain had affected the crops and predicted that grain prices would soar. Therefore, buying interest was unusually strong, with step-by-step competition. It was heard that inland factories in Nanjing and Nantong were also absorbing a lot, totaling between 200 and 300 cars. However, due to the fact that four ships of Australian wheat were traded over the past two days, totaling over 20,000 tons, local merchants took advantage of this opportunity to sell in layers (total daily transaction volume was estimated at over 10 million), about 500 cars' worth. However, with rising public sentiment, it did not soften because of this. Without this batch of selling, speculators' raising of prices would have been unpredictable. Because August is the near month, sellers did not sell, and the increase was the greatest. The remaining increased by only 3 to 5 fen. As a result, this month increased by 3 fen compared to Wednesday, August increased by 7 fen, September increased by 5 fen, October increased by 3 fen, November increased by 2 fen, and December increased by 3 fen. In spot wheat transactions, the price for return to standard was high, and the quoted price also increased by 3 to 5 fen. Fuxin handled 1,400 bags of wheat from Benniu, Danyang, Yangzhou, Pudong, Kunshan, Zhoupu, Jiading, Huangdu, Shuangfeng, etc., and Huafeng handled 2,500 bags.

Silk and Tea: New York Raw Silk Market Active but Unsaleable 186

The climate in New York this summer is extremely hot. Silk factories cannot operate and have successively stopped for summer vacation early. The raw silk market is stagnant due to inactive factory sales. Except for Japanese silk, raw silk from China, Italy, and France has been unsaleable for two weeks. Silk prices have fallen across the board. Shanghai factories have fallen by 3 to 4 jiao per pound, Japanese silk has fallen by 2 to 3 jiao, and Italian silk has also fallen by about 3 jiao. Therefore, silk sales in Shanghai Port have not improved.

Silk Sales in Europe and America Are Almost Stagnant 187

Sales of Chinese silk from European and American markets are stagnant. There has been no transfer of silk telegrams to Shanghai, and the market atmosphere is listless. Yesterday, only Weicheng imported 10 bales of Shanghai white filature, and Kechang and others imported 18 bales of yellow coarse silk. Prices were firm.

Luzhuang Green Tea Sales to Europe Continue to Be Brisk 188

Yesterday, the tea market for foreign firms in this port saw brisk sales of Luzhuang needle tea, eyebrow tea, and superior eyebrow tea to Europe. Major merchants from Wuyuan also sold their goods as soon as they arrived, and the market was not lonely. Gaozhuang Zhenmei, Baochang, Yongxing, and other firms resumed their interest in buying, but their bids were too low. Chinese tea merchants insisted on not selling. Therefore, there were still no large transactions. Currently, the market's Qihong reserves are no more than 14,000 ji, and green tea reserves are no more than 110,000 boxes. The amounts are not large.

Piece Goods: Dong Pi (Japanese Piece Goods) from the Yangtze River Continue to Be Shipped 189

Since the boycott of Japanese goods began, piece goods have become highly sought after. In recent years, Japanese goods have accounted for 80 to 90 percent of piece goods. Strict boycotts have severely impacted Japanese merchants. Although Chinese people have gradually paid attention to the dyeing and weaving industry, the scale is relatively small, and supply cannot meet demand. Therefore, local merchants have been searching for spot goods since the Korean Incident. Sales have been even more brisk than during last year's soaring gold prices. After all the reserves were exhausted, Osaka rushed to ship goods to Shanghai, and sales were quite good. Yesterday, merchants from Sichuan, Hubei, Hunan, and Shantou were still shipping goods. Because this street has detained a lot of goods in recent days, they no longer dare to try. Prices have gradually weakened. Yesterday, Yuehua class fell by 2.5 li. Zhongbing's "Heavenly Yang Guifei" was 2 qian and 4 fen, and Wakayama black floral was 2 qian and 4.5 fen. Lao Hua's straight tribute flannel was exceptionally popular. Although it was 4 qian and 2.5 fen yesterday, there were no spot goods. Lao Hua's dark-colored Ting once ran out of stock and has now been successively arriving in Shanghai. However, the boycott is strict, and it cannot be sold. Because Western goods have few reserves, even if sales of Eastern goods are hindered, they are still not active.

Monochrome Raincoat Fabric Is Uniquely Popular 190

The market for woolens and flannels has not seen much activity recently. Goods from Tongtai, Mitsui, Iwai, etc., have been affected by the boycott. Although the prices are low, there are still few buyers. However, with continuous heavy rain, the sales of raincoat fabric have become very active. The price of single-sided open water beauty is firm, averaging 5 taels and 2 qian per yard for each brand. Monochrome fabrics are scarce and popular. The asking price for the top grade of thin woolen fabric is 3 taels and 7 qian, and the second grade is 3 taels and 3 qian. Single-layer bald blue must add 3 to 4 qian. The prices of yarn surfaces are not greatly fluctuating. Madase flat uniform is priced at 1 tael, 6 qian, and 7.5 fen. Taihe double-sided sand is 3 taels and 4 qian, silk dotted flowers and iridescent colors are 3 taels and 6.5 qian, and double-sided open water beauty is 6 taels and 6 qian.

Dried and Fresh Goods: New Xiang Lotus Seeds Set to Debut Soon 191

Yesterday, according to a letter from Hankou, a batch of new Xiang lotus seeds had arrived in Hankou, totaling 13 boxes of Hengzhou goods, which were purchased by Shanghai firms. The price per dan was 29 taels and 4 qian, and the cost per dan, including handling, was 50 taels. It will be shipped from the origin and is expected to arrive in Shanghai soon. It is predicted that the initial selling price will not be out of line.

Coal: The Coal Market Is Relatively Stable 192

Since the Wanbaoshan Incident, the work of refusing goods has become increasingly tense. Orders for Japanese goods have been occasionally suspended, so the coal market also shows signs of unease. Market prices have risen across the board. However, because it is summer, all uses have decreased, and sales are not smooth. In addition, warehouses are full of stock. Although firms have been quoting prices every day, the number of transactions is not large. Except for the slight purchase of No. 3 coal by out-of-port merchants, local firms and shops are still rarely buying, so the market is relatively stable.

Social News

Turkey Queen 211

— Zhu Yuxiang

American Businesswoman

Famous Far and Wide

In Idaho, USA, there is currently a woman whose name is well-known to everyone in the state, regardless of age or gender, and they respectfully call her the Turkey Queen.

Six years ago, she was like many other farmers' wives, diligently raising a few turkeys in her spare time, selling them for money to supplement the family income and help her husband make a living. However, now, due to her business talent and hard work, she has become a leader of a business association. The members affiliated with that association total 1,800 people, and the total annual trade volume exceeds US$750,000. In addition, the most praiseworthy point is that under her leadership, 1,400 American farm women have been able to obtain economic benefits.

In the spring of 1924, in Boise, Idaho, USA, a Mrs. Brink first proposed establishing a turkey market. In that area, this was simply an innovation, as it had never been done before. The motive for the proposal was that her small flock of turkeys, which she had raised that year, was ready for sale after growing up, but there was not a single buyer in sight. At the same time, hundreds of other farm women were also experiencing the same difficulty. So she thought, why not organize a public group to sell local turkeys together? In this way, large quantities of turkeys could be contracted and sold at good prices to markets in the East and South.

After spending a lot of time and effort, Mrs. Brink's plan finally came to fruition. When this turkey business association was first established, there were only fourteen core members. In the first year after its establishment, the turkeys sold to the Eastern market only filled three freight cars. However, the price obtained broke all previous records for the price of Idaho turkeys. In general, families that raised turkeys received an unexpected bumper harvest.

In the second year, the turkey business association sold several times more turkeys than the previous year, filling twelve freight cars. In the third year, it increased to twenty-seven cars, and in the fourth year, it actually filled forty-six cars. According to a recent survey, between 1930 and 1931, the association transported a full sixty-five freight cars of turkeys out of the state. The total annual trade volume exceeded US$750,000. Moreover, last year's national turkey market prices in the United States were all based on the Idaho Turkey Association's regulations, which shows its market-manipulating power.

The turkey association established by Mrs. Brink is now very developed. The turkey-raising families affiliated with it are not only limited to Idaho, but also extend to the eastern part of Oregon and the southern parts of Idaho. Most of the members, nearly 90 percent, are farm women. Under the leadership of Mrs. Brink, these women know to pay considerable attention to raising turkeys. They are familiar with a special method that allows them to select superior varieties of turkeys and to breed flocks with minimal consumption. Currently, Mrs. Brink's family alone sells more than 1,500 turkeys each year.

Rome to Open Population Problem Conference 212

Nominally Academic Research, Actually Political Significance

Rome Dispatch: The first conference on population problems is scheduled to be held in Rome from September 7th to 10th. Mussolini himself will serve as chairman, with the support and establishment of Professor Gini of the University of Rome, President of the Italian Central Statistical Institute. It is nominally for academic research on population issues in various countries, but in reality, it has political significance.

Japan to Export 12,000 Tons of Coal Slag 213

Sold to Dingsin Company

Tokyo Dispatch: The Gas By-Products Company, an affiliate of Tokyo Gas, is currently planning to export coal slag to China and Southeast Asia. It has already signed a contract with the Sino-German joint-venture steel company, New Company, in Shanghai, to sell 12,000 tons of coal slag, starting in August and to be delivered in six months.

Japan Can Be Called a Bicycle Kingdom 214

5 Million Bicycles Nationwide, Over 24,000 Manufacturing and Repair Shops

According to the Eastern News, the manufacturing and use of bicycles in Japan has been expanding year by year, presenting a surprising phenomenon. The total number of bicycles nationwide in 1913 was 487,076. By 1924, this had increased to 3,675,359, and by December 1930, it had further increased to over 5 million. The use of bicycles by Japanese people is probably the most widespread among all countries. For example, France, the birthplace of the bicycle, only had 223,020 bicycles in 1894. In the United States, except for motorcycles, ordinary bicycles have long disappeared from the streets. The number of bicycles in the UK is almost equal to the number of automobiles. Germany has more bicycles than automobiles. Although the use of automobiles in Japan is gradually increasing, the use of bicycles still has a tendency to expand. According to a 1924 survey, there were as many as 14,214 bicycle manufacturing and repair shops nationwide. The total annual value of the bicycle manufacturing industry is 241.5 million Japanese yen, and it is predicted that it will expand to 300 million yen within five years, becoming one of Japan's largest industries. The United States is called the "Automobile Kingdom," Japan can be called the "Bicycle Kingdom."

Soviet Russia Rejects Foreign Business Influence in Coastal Provinces 215

Preparing to Implement Five-Year Plan

Vladivostok Dispatch: The Soviet Russian government has unilaterally terminated the contract with the Swiss transportation company, White Leine Company, based in Vladivostok. According to observations in business and political circles, this move by the Russian government is intended to maximize the expulsion of foreign commercial firms in the coastal provinces, in order to implement the Five-Year Economic Plan in the Russian Far East.

Life of Working Women in New York 216

— Lin

(7) Life Sketches

A light drink can be bought from the drugstore downstairs, tell them to send it upstairs. Mamie and Brad drink it several times. The young people dancing here don't drink intoxicating liquor. Perhaps they are too poor to buy that kind of expensive wine. Many of them are also very clean.

When midnight arrives, the music stops, which makes the young people exceptionally sad. They ask for one more dance, and sometimes the band agrees.

When it's time to go home, Mamie feels very tired. She has been standing in the store all day, and dancing for several hours in the evening. Now she craves sleep. She is too tired to talk to Brad. He says to her in simple tones, "Beautiful music," "You are a wonderful dance partner."

The two of them arrive at Mamie's door together. Everyone in the house is fast asleep, so they must be very quiet. Brad, of course, can't go inside, because all the rooms in the shared apartment, except for the kitchen, are used as bedrooms. The two of them whisper outside the door for a moment. Mamie says goodnight and puts the key in the lock.

"Mamie," Brad grips her jade arm. "Kiss me, I'm crazy about you."

"Brad, don't, give it up, you absolutely can't do this," Mamie struggles, battling with her own thoughts.

"Just one kiss will do," he pleads. She turns her head and imprints a kiss on his cheek, then she runs into the house.

Mamie has to take off her clothes in the dark, because her sisters are sleeping very soundly. Mamie still feels her lips on Brad's cheek. She has already kissed him. Although she is very tired, she still can't fall asleep immediately. She starts to wonder what she is going to encounter. Is she going to marry someone like Brad? A small shared apartment, working at home all day, and children - that is mostly her destiny - like what her mother encountered. But with Brad, sometimes she feels very sweet, and sometimes she feels very fulfilled, which makes her have passionate dreams. Or will she continue to work in the store - perhaps in a few years, she will be able to get an important position. She has to get up early the next morning, overthinking will inevitably lead to insomnia. She puts her head on the soft pillow, and in an instant, she leaves this real world.

Youth Corner

Where Did She Go? 217

— Mansheng

It was a clear summer morning.

Orange-yellow light flickered in the trees, and the birds chattered on the branches.

He jumped off the tram carrying a pack of Japanese pastries, excitedly walking to the door of No. 39 South Luce Lee. This was it. A faint tremor suddenly rose in his heart. He stopped, hesitating for a while like this. After all, he still raised his head, puffed out his chest, and strode in.

A distressing scene revealed itself before his eyes, which he would never forget, until the moment his soul was lost.

The door of the garret was open, and there was nothing inside except for a heavy iron bed. He was stunned.

On the door, a strip of paper was swaying in the breeze. He went closer to look and saw that it was left for Miss Yi, probably saying that she had also moved away... His eyes suddenly blurred, and every word on the paper seemed to jump. "Anyway, she moved. What's the use of thinking about it?" He thought this way, and at the same time, his sight shifted direction.

He looked around with melancholy, his mind also starting to spin non-stop. Ah, wasn't there a bookshelf here? Wasn't there a desk over there? Wasn't there a photo of her standing on the desk? Ah, the bed, wasn't a tired young woman's sleeping face revealed on this bed four days ago? Happy memories suddenly invaded his mind. He was fantasizing.

Early in the morning four days ago, he stood straight in front of the door of the garret, making an effort to lift his slightly trembling right hand, and lightly tapped on the door.

"Who is it?"

"It's me. Aren't you up yet?... It's nothing..."

... He said haltingly.

"Wait for me to open it," came a sound from inside. She was opening the door.

"Wait a moment before coming in."

"Uh."

She hurriedly burrowed back into the quilt.

He finally went in.

"Good Morning," he said casually.

"............" She smiled.

Her sleepy eyes opened and closed lively, and her wavy hair was scattered on the pillow... All of the beauty of a young woman was reflected in his eyes, in his mind, directly reaching the depths of his heart.

"Sit down," a nightingale-like tone called him back from his daydream.

Page 22

"Yes... Don't be polite," he answered, at a loss.

He sat down. Silence occupied everything. He struggled to say as much as he wanted to say to her, but in the end, it was stopped by his trembling lips.

He began to break the silence in the room.

"I went to see a movie with Mr. Shi last night. Because it was too late, I didn't have time to go back to school, so I slept at his place. Today, I happened to come by..." He seemed to be explaining his intention in coming, talking non-stop.

"Which one?"

"Apollo. The movie wasn't very good."

There was silence again for a while.

"Let's go to see a movie on Sunday. Wait for me here," he was pleading.

"Okay."

The conversation started like this.

They talked like this for a while.

"Go out for a moment, let me get up," she said to him with a smile.

"Okay." Naturally, he walked out with a smile.

She was washing up.

He was always staring at her or her photo in a daze. Suddenly, he took out a Parker pen and a small notebook from his pocket, writing with a rustling sound.

Hot blood rolled like burning,

Life drifted like duckweed,

Revealing a little of the bitterness of life,

The universe is so dim,

The world is so unfair,

Conflict, ah, struggle,

That is the path we should take,

While your youth still exists,

While your blood has not yet congealed,

This final struggle, ah,

Cling tightly to your entire life,

"That's not very good."

He finally handed it to her.

"Very good."

"That one."

Old events, like a movie, flashed through his mind one by one. He couldn't support it any longer. He lowered his head and walked down the stairs in disappointment.

The landlady was washing clothes.

"Where did Miss Ke go?"

"Went back. Isn't she from the western province?"

"When?"

"Yesterday at four o'clock."

"Hmm."

Slow steps carried the heavy body slowly out of the house. He sighed very weakly.

The sun had passed through the trees and shone on the roof, and the birds had stopped singing. People were hurrying to their work. He still kept his head down, his hands in his coat pockets, wandering aimlessly back and forth on Avenue A, seemingly humming very softly, "When I awake to found you gone Ramona, I need you my own!"

Chinese Class 218

— Li Zuoyou

"Mr. Chen, it's a holiday today. Excuse the class," said Duo Yan as soon as he saw Mr. Chen come to class. Originally, today was supposed to be a holiday as usual, but for some reason, there was no notice about the holiday in the notice box. The students didn't have the courage to ask the director to excuse the class, so they had to take a step back and attack the easygoing teacher.

"No, no," Mr. Chen said, shaking his head.

"Ah, just be easygoing. Anyway, our hearts aren't in it," Kai continued to plead.

"What's the point of excusing the class? Why don't we tell a funny story?"

"Good, good," Kai, who wanted to excuse the class, said.

"During the Qingming Festival, it rains heavily... Who can complete the whole poem?" Mr. Chen said with a face full of spring breeze.

"Mr. Chen, I'll continue a line," Huai said, but Mr. Chen just shook his head and waved his hand, not saying a word.

"I'll continue two lines, okay?" Li thought that Mr. Chen's silence meant yes, so he pressured Mr. Chen to answer.

But Mr. Chen still didn't say a word, because his purpose was to have the whole poem completed. One or two lines didn't have much meaning.

Later, Ke raised his hand, but Mr. Chen didn't notice him, so he didn't greet him. He had no choice but to put down his hand.

"Who can write the whole poem?"

"Hey, raise your hand quickly, the teacher is asking someone to go out and write it," Li said to Ke, but Ke didn't raise his hand. He became anxious. He directly pointed at Ke and said to the teacher, "He knows, he knows." He also said to Ke, "Hey, write it quickly. After you write it, we can excuse the class."

Ke wrote on the blackboard, probably because of the magic of the word "Excuse."

Mr. Chen looked at the blackboard and read a poem. The words of the poem were like this:

"During the Qingming Festival, it rains heavily. The traveler on the road is on the verge of despair. May I ask where there is a tavern? A shepherd boy points to the Apricot Blossom Village."

"Who can punctuate it?"

"I know," Si said.

"I know, I know," Ding, nicknamed "Strange Man," said urgently. He didn't care which one the teacher had allowed, and rushed to punctuate it. Si let him.

"Huh, ,,," The classmates saw that he had rushed out to punctuate it, which was too rude, and his punctuation didn't seem very suitable for the poem, so they all ridiculed him with sarcasm.

"That's right, he punctuated it as a Ci poem," Mr. Chen said.

The classroom was suddenly quiet for a few seconds, but soon the atmosphere of "Excuse" filled the classroom again. They were going to attack the teacher again.

"Ah, it's written well, and it's punctuated well. When are we going to excuse the class?" Si said.

"No, no."

"You didn't excuse any classes last semester. Let's excuse it today, consider it your treat, okay?" Da said.

"Ha, ha, you haven't even treated me yet, and now you want me to treat you? Ha, ha, it's really one generation worse than the last. In the past, when you were a disciple, you had to have wine and food to treat the teacher. Ha, ha," Mr. Chen laughed so hard that he couldn't stand up straight. The students also laughed along with Mr. Chen in a disruptive manner. They knew that in this kind of situation, if they laughed like this, although it was somewhat inappropriate, the teacher would definitely not treat them with harsh words and expressions.

Kai hadn't spoken for a long time. At this time, his tongue had already been jumping, ready to issue a mobilization order. He said with a mischievous tone, "Um, Mr. Chen, I heard that the steamed pork buns in the kitchen taste pretty good. How about we go and order the buns now?" He ran towards the door like he was charging. The students near the door also rushed out the door. But Mr. Chen hurriedly stopped the students who were about to rush out but hadn't rushed out yet. He didn't know what to say. He became anxious, and just quickly waved both hands left and right in front of his chest, his face looking like he was angry but not angry, like he was smiling but not smiling. He used his hands to stop them, not letting them go outside. The students who hadn't left the door, because they were stopped by Mr. Chen, and if they did this, the teacher would be terribly angry, so they all retreated like defeated soldiers.

Mr. Chen saw that they had sat down, and then said,

"Um, listen."

"Um, listen," the students followed Mr. Chen and said, because Mr. Chen's "Listen" contained a special tone and meaning. But Mr. Chen ignored them and continued,

"Today, we'll talk about Zhu Guangqian's 'Talking about Movement'."

"Teacher, form is emptiness, and emptiness is form. But when we haven't yet understood what form is, how can we know what emptiness is? So before talking about movement, we should excuse a class, let us experience what movement is, and then talk about theoretical movement," said Wei, nicknamed "Literary Man."

"Um, that's right, that's right," everyone shouted like they were cheering.

"No, no, we can't excuse the class now, because..."

Before Mr. Chen could finish speaking, they listened again, "Yes, yes," and they began their second charge.

Da, who was closest to the door, got up and opened the door. They all rushed out together as if they had prepared for it. By the time Mr. Chen wanted to stop them, it was already too late, because most of the people had already left. Mr. Chen had no choice but to smile, shake his head, take the loose-leaf anthology, put on his already changed-looking woolen hat, and talk and laugh with the students who hadn't left yet, slowly walking out of the classroom door.
